<rating>5</rating>< review>
The phone answerer, Bridgette, asked only a few questions about what needed fixing, a bathtub faucet leaking problem. The questions seemed only relevant to their own need to provide us with a quick response to get the job done well, and within that call she said Roto-Rooter could have a plumber there within an hour. She had a very friendly manner in her voice and personality. I told her many found our residence hard to locate, so advised her to tell the person coming to fix the leaking faucets to call me when he got to the nearest well known street intersection. It was a pleasant surprise to hear his phone call to me within 30 minutes, then I got in my little car and met him to escort the Roto-Rooter truck to our ranch, and our permanent foundation modular house, a Champion made in 1988. Roto Rooter had replaced all of the plastic water pipes circa 1995 with copper pipes and stainless steel flex cables to almost every outlet. This has made the house almost trouble free since then. The plumber arrived smiling and totally ready to go to work. He took apart the ailing old tub valve stems, showed my wife and I how they'd disintegrated over time since the manufacture of the house. He was almost immediately able to come up with an exact price of what the fix would cost. Returning from a run to town to get the parts, he took out a much larger box of tools, and he did the replacing of both valves with brand new ones taking about 15 minutes (he had gone to town to find the somewhat unusual modular house parts). Allen, the plumber, had accepted a root beer I'd given him since the day was so hot, but upon leaving I noticed he had left the big glass half full, so intent he had been upon fixing our problem quickly. He and I worked together to adjust the rubber seals, me turning the house water supply valve on and off quickly for his adjusting in the tub, and my wife even gave him an old grommet she had from where she works that proved helpful. The complete professionalism of Roto-Rooter in doing everything they said they would do, and doing it fast caused me in saying goodby to Allen, "Thanks for the fast fix and the high competence of your work." Working with them was actually fun, since every other plumbers we had called seemed almost afraid of doing modular and mobile home cases.< /review>

Had a broker later line in my second home in Hemet. Called "7" plumbers who advertised 24/7 plumbing service. Five of these companies made "excuses" of why they could not come out that night at 12 midnight. The 6th company said they had a man already out in the field and he would not be finished for "at least" 2 hours and it might have to wait till the morning. We called two of the Roto Router Offices trying to locate a plumber and the answering service noted that both of our calls were for the same address (indicating they have a good tracking system), The answering service lady indicated she would call the service man on call and get back to me "shortly" in about 10 minutes. Sure enough ten minutes late Joe T. called and asked questions about the problem, size of the broke pipe (to be sure he had parts in the truck) or he would had to run to the service center to pick up parts. I explain the problem, gave him the measurement of the pipe size (attempted to take a photo but it was too wet and dark even with a flash). He said he would come out and should arrive in about 15 minutes. HE ARRIVED IN 15 MINUTES.
As it turned out Joe T. is the "supervisor" and the man on call was not there and this was the third night in a row that Joe T. went out for somebody else. He was very polite, pleasant, knowledgeable and quick to diagnose the problem. They was a time delay due to my lot unfortunately did not have a water shut off value from the street. An unfortunate complication, we had looked and so did the the subdivision manager and grounds manager before we even called the plumber. So the entire subdivision water had to be shut down. Once that was completed Joe T. Fixed the problem in about 15 minutes. The bill was slightly expense, but for the time of night and quick response, it was "very reasonable". This excellent rating is mainly because of this companies good backup supervisor who really deserves the credit. If he wasn't there for backup, this might be an entirely different review. Yeah Joe T. REALLY GOOD JOB!
So if you call Roto Rooter in Hemet and you can't get the main service guy, be sure to tell them you wish to speak with Joe T.<//Text>

(Original)
WARNING!!  DO NOT TAKE YOUR DOG TO THIS GROOMER!
I was looking for a simple nail clip. I was in the area and found this place (I should have read the reviews).

They took my dog inside and told me to wait for 10 min. The lady that attended me kept coming outside to meet with people (her family I believe) and she kept telling me "just one more min". 30 minutes passed and no sign of my dog. I called and asked her to take the dog even if she did not clip the nails.

I could not believe what I saw when they brought my dog out. His nails were not only poorly clipped, but bleeding! In the picture, you can see the amount of the yellow powder they put to avoid the bleed.

When I confronted the lady, she told me "this is normal"- "all dogs bleed". I understand the bleeding of one or two nails, but ALL OF THEM? come on!! My dog is now limping and unable to walk.

No-one has ever made my dog bleed! ever!

I refused to pay, because the basic condition for this service is to 1. have nails properly clipped and 2. avoid injury to a dog - and both of this basic conditions were not met. The lady that attended me followed me to my car and kept recording me. I was harassed and threatened.

Believe me when I say that this was by far the worst service I have ever experienced in my life!

Is Shabu Shabu worth $25? It's definitely not my everyday lunch budget but when the occasions come, that $25 should be worth a lot of excitement. I didn't feel like there was much to get excited about at Joon Shabu 2 - the food was good, service was okay, but nothing really stood out to make me want to come back. I would still default to my long-time favorite Dada for group lunches, where we can all drown our feelings in unlimited soup and devour all types of meats and seafoods for the same cost.

My boyfriend and I shared a Tonkotsu broth with 10oz Australian lamb.
We ordered a large one-person meal because we weren't hungry enough to get a Shared entree (14oz meat, 2 servings of vegetables, $40 price tag). I thought the Tonkotsu broth smelled better than it tasted because the flavor tasted pretty weak. The meat was good, and I really liked dipping it in the sesame/goma sauce which I wish was less diluted. My favorite part of the meal was the red rice. It was the perfect texture, and it was so good I could've just ate that alone and called it a day.

The service was friendly, although kind of slow. Since we had a large group, it's hard to get everyone served at the same time. It was also weird that half our table got our bills processed and we had to wait another few minutes for the rest of our party get their bills before we could leave.<//review>

<rate>4</rate><Text>High-end Chinese fusion in Agoura Hills? I'm in!

Mandarin Lotus is located right off the 101 freeway on Kanan Road. I never knew this place existed until my friend started raving about it a few weekends ago at the Chili Cook Off. Based on what she said, I knew I needed to go check it out. I was not disappointed.

To my surprise, this restaurant was established in 1988. Formerly known as Mandarin Express, this restaurant specializes in Michelin-inspired Eurasian cuisine, with unique molecular gastronomy techniques and recipes. Fusion recipes include tastes from many cuisines, including French, Spanish, and Thai, to name a few. Their ingredients are definitely high quality and fresh.

I've been here a couple times now, and both times were excellent. This is definitely elevated Chinese cuisine, and they have very interesting items on the menu. Their menu is actually huge, with countless options to choose from ranging from low price to very expensive high-end. I've only been for lunch, so I've only gone cheap with the broccoli beef lunch special, but I am curious about a number of their other items. I will say, the broccoli beef is very good here, and the rice is cooked to perfection.

If you've never been, I'd definitely say this is a worthwhile restaurant to visit if you're in the area. Service is very nice, but maybe not the quickest. They do cook all of their food fresh to order, so this isn't much of a complaint, just a heads up to those in a rush. Due to the proximity to my office, I'll likely be back soon. Go ahead and give it a try for yourself!< /Text>< pictures>

< Review>
The menu here is extensive, and every dish is cooked to order fresh. As someone with multiple food allergies, I appreciated the fact that the dishes were fully customizable since they are made to order- I knew I had nothing to worry about from an allergy standpoint.

We came tonight (Father's Day) as a large group with multiple, let's just say, difficult personalities. Although the service was a little slow, it was only one person working front of house, one working the back, so they absolutely were doing the best they could. Patience paid off, as the food was absolutely delicious. There was not a single dish that was off in any way shape or form. In fact, a couple of the dishes were made with vegetarian meat, and 2 beef conissuers accidentally ate one of the mock beef dishes and had no idea they did- it was that good.  In the future, with a large group, I may consider ordering to go, but as I mentioned, patience pays off dining in. Looking forward to returning in the future.< /Review>

< review>
So, this is my seventh year living in Oak Park, and the first time that I've been to this amazing hole in the wall restaurant!    I'd always been vaguely aware of this nondescript restaurant - it's squeezed in a tiny space in a strip mall,  near the karate center, Nick Rail's music,  behind the IHOP, and way behind the Jack in the Box at the corner of Kanan and the 101 off-ramp.  I guess it was the "Express" in the name which made me think it was something like "Panda Express" - take out pseudo-Chinese junk food.  Or maybe it was the small restaurant space and buffet-like store counter which you can see through the front windows, also reminiscent of a fast food take out restaurant.  Panda Express it most definitely is not.  Mandarin Express is of all things a fancy gourmet restaurant!   Chinese-Mediterranean-Californian fusion food.   They take some basic Chinese food ingredients and cook it with a variety of vegetables and spices from around the world. You can eat an all-vegetarian meal here!  There's an entire page of mock duck/chicken/shrimp/pork dishes.   But their shrimp and other meat dishes are terrific too.  The food just bursts with multiple flavors in your mouth.  I really think they should re-name the place, or at least take out the "Express" part from the name.  It just doesn't do the place justice.  The owner-cooks are really friendly too.  A great place to take your best friends and family!< /review>

<Pictures>None< /Pictures><Resp>{'time': 1529082728015, 'text': 'Thank you Shawn, we look forward to seeing you again soon!'}</Resp>< Text>
My son went here a lot when he lived in the area. So he chose it for his birthday dinner. When we got there it was obvious the owners knew him and had missed him. They asked about one of his friends that had passed away. In fact everyone that came in that night gave and received personal and warm greetings. It was like a family gathering.

What could inspire such happiness beyond cordial friendliness?

The food! It was close your eyes and luxuriate awesome!

While my son and I noticed changes to the orange chicken, it was still delicious. This is not a static restaurant. It's fusion. They learn and incorporate from a variety of food cultures. So the OC (which BTW we never found in China) they reimagined was great - no skimping on anything.

We tried the shrimp they recommended but declined to eat it shell and all (if you've been to China you know about exoskeleton delicacies - a taste we haven't acquired). But even though we took off the shells, the seasoning was too incredible not to nibble off from the usually discarded shell. And the seasoning on the included vegetables led to who gets the last one squabbles.

Mongo beef - great. Cashew chicken- great. Chicken fried rice - ok anywhere else but with how everything else was spiced to perfection it suffered by comparison but was still enjoyable.

There were many other artistic and culinary touches that enhanced the food experience. This is not a decor destination. This is about the food and people dedicated to their craft and growing with it. And genuinely loving it.

My wif and I loved it too. It's now on our list to return in a month for a date night.

I hope you'll try it and love it too.

Be seeing you!< /Text>
